<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1018274866908110869 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1018274866908110869><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=armslegshandsfeet data-user-id=466248882335252500>armslegshandsfeet</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Saturday, September 10, 2022 6:40 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1018274866908110869>9/10/2022 6:40 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>dbt is a great tool. I love using it, and I think it does a lot to enable the analytical pipeline process. But it doesn&#39;t actually model the data for you. I think there&#39;s plenty of space for analysts to rapidly iterate on pipelines for one-offs or prototypes while an analytics engineer develops more performant / cost efficient / reusable models that will get heavier use.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1018318676140769320 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1018318676140769320><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/113128130822021120/0eee50ecf79243635e5cdb858d236296.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=urthor data-user-id=113128130822021120>Urthor</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Saturday, September 10, 2022 9:34 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1018318676140769320>9/10/2022 9:34 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Analytics engineering isn&#39;t new.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1018318690380415037 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1018318690380415037><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, September 10, 2022 9:34 PM">9:34 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>That&#39;s the important thing.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1018318786413219961 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1018318786413219961><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, September 10, 2022 9:35 PM">9:35 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Analytics engineers are just people who are really good with SQL. <div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1020679646708248697 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1020679646708248697><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=armslegshandsfeet data-user-id=466248882335252500>armslegshandsfeet</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Saturday, September 17, 2022 9:56 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1020679646708248697>9/17/2022 9:56 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>To answer your last question first, Snowflake has a web IDE that&#39;s pretty similar to SSMS.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1020680414152626246 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1020680414152626246><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, September 17, 2022 9:59 AM">9:59 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Snowflake architecture is very different from SQL Server. It&#39;s a distributed columnar database. You can read more about the architecture online if you&#39;re interested, but the tldr is that the way it stores and accesses data is more efficient when your queries are mostly aggregations over a few columns.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1020680787210805371 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1020680787210805371><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, September 17, 2022 10:01 AM">10:01 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Snowflake also has some optimization magic with regard to how it partitions the data. This allows you to avoid having to scan an entire table with every query.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1020681045231808584 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1020681045231808584><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, September 17, 2022 10:02 AM">10:02 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>That being said, your analysts can still write bad / expensive queries, and there are manual optimizations you can make.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1021516913983107092 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1021516913983107092><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/113128130822021120/0eee50ecf79243635e5cdb858d236296.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/499104423872823298/1a01884db1516a1f0a2fa9a48ed24947.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=winenose>Lauri</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1021469753853886536')"> The &quot;direction&quot; of those tools is different. <div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1022247175356416050 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1022247175356416050><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/5.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/388363256546459719/68091da0dd05eaf0caa1a78666c05eba.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=nurul15>ライト</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1022222014695620690')"> Hey guys had a quick question about Databricks. Anyone here use it as part of their production pipeline? If so, are you using the notebook UI for coding or some sort of other packaged method? Just trying to understand how the notebook method would work with unit testing, CI/CD etc </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=tholiv5002 data-user-id=843572716552192080>Tholiv</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, September 21, 2022 5:45 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1022247175356416050>9/21/2022 5:45 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>In our case, we use Workflow Jobs to orchestrate notebooks in our Production pipelines.
Some prefer working directly within the Notebooks (source-controlled via Repos), and there is the option to develop locally via IDE. The packaging and unit-testing can be done either as normal software engineering practices (and pushed to Repos) - or it can also be done via scheduled Notebooks as well.
I think these two resources would be helpful to what you are looking for:
<a href="https://docs.databricks.com/dev-tools/index-ide.html">https://docs.databricks.com/dev-tools/index-ide.html</a>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1022287279156383804 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1022287279156383804><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/1.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=aaronistyping data-user-id=1001961672430342234>aaron</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, September 21, 2022 8:24 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1022287279156383804>9/21/2022 8:24 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>It gives you a good overview of the modern tools, so you get a bit of hands on experience with RDBMS: [postgres, mysql, db2], NoSQL databases: [MongoDB, Cassandra, Cloudant], distributed computing technologies [Spark, Airflow, Hadoop], some data warehouse / lake examples, ETL, ELT. There are courses within it on database administration / maintenance, shell scripting, and using python as and using Python glue for these technologies (e.g. database connectors etc).  The course is good at giving you an overview, but you get the most value out of it if you actually install these things on your own machines / servers and play around with them which is what I&#39;ve been doing.  There are some issues with the course that can be frustrating as a learner e.g. the technology they use to host the cloud development environments / labs / exercises was continuously failing and you&#39;d have to wait for a fix. There are also instances where there are mistakes / errors in the course that they really should have fixed. Ultimately, you get out of it what you put in, and I&#39;m grateful for having taken it because it gave me the overview which made me go on to investigate these technologies further.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

Right now I&#39;m in the process of researching how to design a small scale data pipelines with just extraction and ingestion, but the hardest part right now is the use case, I haven&#39;t figured out any scenario for this pipeline

Any ideas on what should be a doable topic for a small personal data pipeline project ? </span> <span class=chatlog__reply-edited-timestamp title="Monday, September 26, 2022 10:42 PM">(edited)</span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=luxi7335 data-user-id=137286287257239552>Luxì</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, September 27, 2022 2:25 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1024190017125503017>9/27/2022 2:25 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>The use case would be getting insights through certain data for yourself or others. Or just to learn something new.

For example I enjoy LoL and using the API you could extract data out of it to do your own insight calculations. I once did it based on username and champion per role, to be able to see the difference between Jax top vs Jax jungle stats or win rates.

That was my project/use case.

Now on to technology, if you want to learn the basics of DE and EL(T) then try to keep it simple, just your scripts and a cron job for scheduling. If you got the basics down, you can look into an orchestration tool like Airflow, Prefect, Dagster, Kestra (<a href="https://github.com/kestra-io/kestra)">https://github.com/kestra-io/kestra)</a>

And/or cloud options to run your code (just use free tier only so you don&#39;t rack up bills ;)) GCP, Azure or AWS. USA has big market in AWS while Europe (or at least the Netherlands) is rather big on Azure.</span></div><div class=chatlog__embed><div class=chatlog__embed-color-pill style=background-color:rgba(30,35,39,255)></div><div class=chatlog__embed-content-container><div class=chatlog__embed-content><div class=chatlog__embed-text><div class=chatlog__embed-title><a class=chatlog__embed-title-link href=https://github.com/kestra-io/kestra><div class="chatlog__markdown chatlog__markdown-preserve">GitHub - kestra-io/kestra: Kestra is an infinitely scalable orchest...</div></a></div><div class=chatlog__embed-description><div class="chatlog__markdown chatlog__markdown-preserve">Kestra is an infinitely scalable orchestration and scheduling platform, creating, running, scheduling, and monitoring millions of complex pipelines. - GitHub - kestra-io/kestra: Kestra is an infini...</div></div></div><div class=chatlog__embed-thumbnail-container><a class=chatlog__embed-thumbnail-link href=https://images-ext-1.discordapp.net/external/PjFq98re6MV_RkCAG3nadXtpmZq-C6gr49qz7eM8bXI/https/repository-images.githubusercontent.com/204164353/984c8eeb-b2f8-40ef-bbd3-cf3c28030a77> <img class=chatlog__embed-thumbnail src=https://images-ext-1.discordapp.net/external/PjFq98re6MV_RkCAG3nadXtpmZq-C6gr49qz7eM8bXI/https/repository-images.githubusercontent.com/204164353/984c8eeb-b2f8-40ef-bbd3-cf3c28030a77 alt=Thumbnail loading=lazy> </a></div></div></div></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=thumbsup><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=👍 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f44d.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>1</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>

Right now I&#39;m in the process of researching how to design a small scale data pipelines with just extraction and ingestion, but the hardest part right now is the use case, I haven&#39;t figured out any scenario for this pipeline

Any ideas on what should be a doable topic for a small personal data pipeline project ? </span> <span class=chatlog__reply-edited-timestamp title="Monday, September 26, 2022 10:42 PM">(edited)</span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=arku10 data-user-id=754580208777953381>arku10</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, September 27, 2022 7:42 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1024450923038257182>9/27/2022 7:42 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>There&#39;s a ton of things you can build a pipeline for, which ironically makes coming up with an idea to do that hard.

A possible idea could be to find a freely available data set online (try kaggle or a dataset of your choice like <a href="https://www.kaggle.com/competitions/titanic/data)">https://www.kaggle.com/competitions/titanic/data)</a> . Read that data onto local, maybe transform it and extract some information. For instance for the dataset I mentioned in the URL you could answer the question &quot;Which age group had the most number of survivors&quot;. This information can then be loaded onto a postgres table for instance.

So,
connect &amp; save dataset to local &gt;&gt; groupby(transform) data &amp; save to disk &gt;&gt; build out insert query &gt;&gt; insert into database table

This is a very simple use case. Just to give you an idea.

Then pick a tool you could use build this pipeline out like <span class="chatlog__markdown-mention" title="luxi7335">@Lux&#236;</span> mentioned - airflow, dagster or Prefect, mage.ai etc. and set off building it.

If this seems overwhelming then simply follow along with the tutorial offered by mage.ai at <a href="https://github.com/mage-ai/mage-ai/blob/master/docs/tutorials/quick_start/etl_restaurant/README.md">https://github.com/mage-ai/mage-ai/blob/master/docs/tutorials/quick_start/etl_restaurant/README.md</a>

case in point: bathroom is stored as decimal, because a toilet-only bathroom would be recognized as <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">0.5</code>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1026286877856239757 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1026286877856239757><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/235288323743154176/05c06b21ad5299ad3dbd59621c677330.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=jon.m7377 data-user-id=235288323743154176>jon.m</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, October 2, 2022 9:17 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1026286877856239757>10/2/2022 9:17 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I’m struggling to understand where data modeling (Kimball, etc) solves problems and where it becomes a slow down. 

In other words, where the line is and how to navigate it.

I’ve recently been on a project where reports were built off of a star schema set up, after source data was ingested and modeled in a DWH.


This created a lot of slow down it seemed, both in terms of development time and in terms of how quickly the data could be updated in the reporting layer.

It would have been easier I think to have by passed the modeling.

I’m often wondering how I can interpret the benefit of data modeling.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1026292493333037197 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1026292493333037197><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/235288323743154176/05c06b21ad5299ad3dbd59621c677330.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=jon.m7377>jon.m</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1026286877856239757')"> I’m struggling to understand where data modeling (Kimball, etc) solves problems and where it becomes a slow down. 

In other words, where the line is and how to navigate it.

I’ve recently been on a project where reports were built off of a star schema set up, after source data was ingested and modeled in a DWH.


This created a lot of slow down it seemed, both in terms of development time and in terms of how quickly the data could be updated in the reporting layer.

It would have been easier I think to have by passed the modeling.

I’m often wondering how I can interpret the benefit of data modeling. </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=armslegshandsfeet data-user-id=466248882335252500>armslegshandsfeet</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, October 2, 2022 9:39 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1026292493333037197>10/2/2022 9:39 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Data modeling has a number of advantages, but for me, the biggest are source abstraction and the ability to gracefully handle multiple versions of history.

As to the first, your consumers don&#39;t have to worry about how you&#39;re constructing something like a customer dim; maybe it&#39;s a single object from Salesforce, or maybe it&#39;s 15+ sources between SaaS objects, Kafka topics, and raw product tables. All they need to care about are the attributes the dimension exposes.

As to the second, SCD2 tables give you a very easy way of looking at attributes at different points in time. Want to know what the regions looked like at the time of the sale? Or do you want to know what those regions look like in the present day? This requires very little work with the proper modeling, especially in comparison to how you&#39;d handle something like this with OBT.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

I think that use case is very clear. Thank you for the insight!</span></div></div></div></div></div>
